Figure 6.32: Area under the curve (AUC) of the averaged three best optimized models.
6.8
Discussion
In this project, Gaussian Optimization was utilized to select the best set of hyper-
parameters on three diﬀerent models. With a surrogate objective function and by
deﬁning a probability range for the best set of hyperparameters based from previous
trials. The optimized models were then tested in the same test set. The results pre-
sented in Table 6.3, where the performance metrics for the baseline and optimized
models are confronted. Suggest hoe the optimization had no eﬀect for the model’s im-
provements. By contrast, a decrease in performance was noted after the optimization
of 5000 trials. Although, an the number of trials becomes a signiﬁcant discriminate
for the optimization process. The training and validation loss required more than
==PAGE:116==
88
6 Learning Algorithm
20000 iterations for the validation loss achieve a plateau. Therefore, an increase in
number of trials, equivalent to the number of iterations can result in a maximisation
of the loss with signiﬁcant improvements.
Additionally, the user-deﬁne range for the selection of hyperparameters becomes a
constraint. A workﬂow to consider, might be shifting the user-deﬁned hyperparameter
range to a narrower range closer to the best selection from previous trials. However,
the increase on trials and user-deﬁne range, increases the computational time of the
optimization process. However, when the model for both gender is trained with no
early stop and a maximum number of iterations of 200000 as shown in Figure 6.10;
no signiﬁcant improvements are observe on the validation loss, while the training loss
increases in our maximization problem.
The results presented in the ROC curves for the three models (Figures 6.16, 6.24,
and 6.32) shows that the model had less discriminator characteristics for the normal
and mild, whereas the classes moderate and severe obtained the leading AUC. The
confusion matrix for all models in Figure 6.33, indicates similar miss classiﬁcations.
This results, might convey the presence of less random and more signiﬁcant response
of the patients with moderate and severe, than patients diagnosed with normal or mild.
Figure 6.33: Confusion matrix of the averaged three best optimized models for (a) both
gender model, (b) male model, and (c) female model.
Future work could be dedicate to the prediction of AHI as a regression problem.
Although, the model’s complexity might drastically increase. A two-class problem
might be considered, although diagnosis would be too broad in terms of AHI in order
to produce an accurate diagnosis.
==PAGE:117==
6.9 Conclusion
89
6.9
Conclusion
This chapter introduced the methods and theoretical concepts necessary to under-
stand how to interpret and optimize the eXtreme Gradient Boosting (XGB) model.
The proposed study for OSA classiﬁcation uses boosting decisions tree and create
diﬀerent models based on gender in order to observe signiﬁcant characteristics. The
model did not achieved good performance with accuracy metrics bellow 50% on un-
seen data from the same studies.
==PAGE:118==
90
==PAGE:119==
CHAPTER 7
Discussion
This chapter concludes the thesis, the proposed methods had been discussed through-
out the thesis.
Chapter 5 presented the data reduction methods implemented in this study. It
describes how domain knowledge on the data was implemented to obtain better pre-
dictors. Moreover, the diﬀerent algorithm to identify the most relevant predictors for
AHI.
Chapter 6 demonstrated the algorithm of XGB, based on boosting tree methods.
The chapter indicates the methods of the Thesis, and how the studies were performed.
7.1
Conclusion
The main objective of this Thesis was to render the Alliance Sleep Questionnaire
(ASQ) into a proper tabular structure for the implementation of a ML algorithm.
With an initial shape of 700 predictors of mixed data types, and a notorious time
gap between the AHI labels and the ASQ completion date. The adaption was accom-
plished by performing manual data wrangling and transformation to determine the
best format for the predictors. Moreover, data sparsity was considered and questions
with similar information were merged to reduce the dimensionality. In addition, the
precise management of missing values, coherent to each question type, and to avoid
high bias was study carefully. Table 5.3 demonstrate the impact of the this methods.
Feature importance algorithms as MI and ANOVA test convey information in
accordance to medical knowledge, on which predictors resulted to be the more sig-
niﬁcant. Loud snoring, weight, use of Sedatives/hypnotics, presence of comorbidities,
presence of seizures, and Multivariable Apnea Prediction (MAP) scores were among
the most relevant. By thresholding the relevance score, feature were reduces into the
most signiﬁcant.
ASQ dataset adaptation for a ML model. The ASQ contains more than 400 ques-
tions, making the model prone to the curse of dimensionality [56]. Also, the branching
of the ASQ introduces numerous missing values that are not discriminate values for
==PAGE:120==
92
7 Discussion
ML models.
The model was trained with three diﬀerent subsets of the 2817 subjects. The pro-
posed models splits the dataset subsets into train (70%), validation (20%), and test
(10%). The ﬁrst model considers the complete dataset and obtains an AUC= 0.605. A
second and third model are trained and tested on the basis that OSA aﬀects the pa-
tients diﬀerent based on gender. Consequently, a second model is trained and tested
with only the male subjects and obtains an AUC= 0.654. Lastly, a model with only
female subjects is considered and obtains a AUC= 0.634. Each model is optimized
with Gaussian Optimization to ﬁnd the best set of hyperparameters.
The models demonstrated substandard discriminatory characteristic for the clas-
siﬁcation of normal and mild class.
Whereas, the models performed best in the
classiﬁcation of moderate and severe classes. This results, might convey the presence
of less random and more signiﬁcant response of the patients with moderate and severe,
than patients diagnosed with normal or mild.
7.2
Future Work
There are several possible implementation or conﬁgurations that could potentially
improve the model performance. These ideas are presented below
Hyperparameter search: Introduce longer tuning iterations and utilize the re-
sult from past optimization studies on the ASQ to narrow the hyperparameter space.
Time δ: Select a shorter time diﬀerence (δ) between the ASQ completion date
and the PSG study. The current δ = 365 days. Between the ASQ and PSG, a year
time gap could introduce noise in the measure from the ASQ.
Regression problem: Change the problem’s objective into a regression problem,
where the main objective is the prediction of the AHI as a continuous number. Con-
sideration into the model’s complexity must be carefully tested and regularize.

==PAGE:181==
Source Code
This appendix provides an overview of all code involved in the development of the proposed
mode. The code was written in Python v3.8 [63]. All the ﬁles are classes, the project utilizes
object orienting programming for its execution.
Source Code Description
Preprocessing Classes
• conﬁg.py 1
– Input: static paths and conﬁgurations
– Output: static paths and conﬁgurations
– Description: Conﬁguration dictionary to transfers paths and constant variables
between the classes.
• dictionary_reader.py 2
– Input:ASQ information table
– Output:dictionary of the ASQ information
– Description: The Dictionary_Reader reader class read the complete asq infor-
mation, where the questions and answer options are written.
To be able to
user an automatic detection and identiﬁcation of the questions types, the class
Dictionary_Reader read the table and store the asq information in a dictionary
format. Where, the keys are the questions codes and the values the diﬀerent
possible answers the patient can response.
Useful for the other classes identify the 0 type of question and modify the missing
values.
• asq_added_entries.py 3
– Input: Datasets paths
– Output: merged and cleansed dataset
– Description: Class dedicated to new ASQ observations given from diﬀerent stud-
ies.
Read the ASQ, merge with the AHI. Selecting observations with AHI
values.
Furthermore, extracting the desired columns deﬁned from the Dictio-
nary_Reader keys. Matches the ASQ to the AHI with the nearest date. Lastly,
apply the appropriate pre processing to work with the data
==PAGE:182==
154
Source Code
• data_description.py 4
– Input: Datasets paths
– Output: -
– Description: Class dedicated for describing the dataset, and making statistical
measures.
Model Classes
• main.py 5
– Input: Calls to preprocessing classes and model classes. All the model pipeline
is structed in this class.
– Output: Save the models, evaluations.
– Description: Main Class to run all the models. Feature selection, dataset splits,
training, optimization and plotting are all called in this function.
• dataset.py 6
– Input: conﬁg: dict, stratify: Optional[bool] = False
– Output:dictionary of the ASQ information
– Description: Class dedicate to partition the dataset into the desired classes
• feature_selection.py 7
– Input: conﬁg: dict, predictors: list, dataset: Union[dict, pd.DataFrame] = None
– Output: Most signiﬁcan features
– Description: Class dedicate to apply the feature selection on the dataset. The
class can implemented Mutual Information and ANOVA depending on the called
method. The class is intended to be called in the main class.
• model_deﬁnition_xgboost.py 8
– Input: conﬁg: dict
– Output: Trained model and predictions
– Description: Class dedicate to initialize the XGBoost model. The Class uses
the following methods: get_model: return the model to use with user deﬁned
hyperparameters model_ﬁt: train the and predict on the test data. The methods
call the plotting functions inside the class
• optimizer_optuna.py 9
– Input: dtrain: pd.DataFrame, dvalid: pd.DataFrame, dict_single_params: dict,
dir_save: pathlib.Path, pred: list, target: str, direction: str, sample_weights:
Optional[bool] = False
– Output: Objective value
– Description: Deﬁne the hyperparameters to train, with their ranges. The models
is trained and tested on the validation data. The objective loss is then compute
and the objective value is returned
==PAGE:183==
Preprocessing Classes
155
Preprocessing Classes
1 """
2 Configuration
dictionary
to
transfers
paths

def
get_time_delta_days (asq_date: pd.Series , ahi_date: pd.Series
) -> pd.DataFrame:

"""
356

in days of all the

between

# asq_date = merge_asq_ahi_date [’completed ’]. astype(’

- ahi_date))

def
nearest_date (items: list , pivot):
369
"""
370
Find
the
closest
date , items
are the asq
dates
and
pivot is
the
date of the PSG. Both
inputs
must be
371
in the
same
date
format.
372
# https :// kanoki.org /2022/02/09/ how -to -find -closest -date -in -
dataframe -for -a-given -date/

# https :// stackoverflow .com/questions /32237862/ find -the -

374

items_
in items if

< pivot] ->

# timedelta = abs(nearest
- pivot) # counts
the
number
of
dates
between

pivot
378

mutual_info_classif ,

def
evaluate_model (model , X, y, num_splits : int , num_repeats :

, n_jobs =-1, error_score=’raise ’)
